        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2015/01/09/1356520/-God-Goes-Into-Real-Estate-Now-Owns-Town" id="titleHref">
          God Goes Into Real Estate, Now Owns Town
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/zenbassoon">
          zenbassoon
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=215040&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2015/01/09/1356520/-God-Goes-Into-Real-Estate-Now-Owns-Town" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="God Goes Into Real Estate, Now Owns Town" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2015/01/09/1356520/-God-Goes-Into-Real-Estate-Now-Owns-Town" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="221" data-story_id="1356520" href="/story/2015/01/09/1356520/-God-Goes-Into-Real-Estate-Now-Owns-Town#comments">
           221 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <div class="dkimg-c">
          <span class="image_container">
           <img alt="" height="252" src="http://images.dailykos.com/images/123480/large/jesus_facepalm.jpg?1420774445" width="360"/>
          </span>
         </div>
         <a href="http://www.addictinginfo.org/2015/01/08/god-is-now-the-owner-of-a-town-in-alabama-and-all-hell-is-breaking-loose/">
          Dateline Winfield, Alabama--Because of COURSE it's Alabama:
         </a>
         <p>
          In a secret meeting where only the city council and the mayor were present, it was unanimously decided to cede ownership of the town to that person or persons known as "God".
         </p>
         <p>
          Now, I know what you're thinking. And frankly I agree with you. Here is the text of the resolution:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          Whereas we acknowledge God is the owner of the City of Winfield and that it is a City under God. We acknowledge that at all times, He is in control.
          <p>
           Whereas, we acknowledge that through His leadership, the Mayor and City Council will seek his wisdom and knowledge to be good stewards of the city.
          </p>
          <p>
           Whereas, we acknowledge that though prayer, with His guidance and presence, that we will be able to trust that no problem will be too large or too small to overcome.
          </p>
          <p>
           Whereas, we acknowledge that the City of Winfield is where it is today because of Gods grace and mercy.
          </p>
          <p>
           Whereas, we acknowledge that at all times and in all circumstances, His will shall be done.
          </p>
          <p>
           Whereas, we acknowledge that to God be the glory.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <iframe defang_allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/HQfzwFloVqA" width="560">
         </iframe>
         <p>
          But wait. It gets worse. When asked about any objections to this based on that little thing called the Establishment Clause, the mayor had this to say:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          Im going to step on a lot of peoples toes but theres not but one God and, that one God, to Him be the glory. Theres no other way; theres no other God. There are a lot of religions out there but only one God.
         </blockquote>
         Now to me, that sounds a lot like "There is no God but God." And I'm sure if we pointed out those consistencies to him he would get red in the face.
         <p>
          Anyway, one anonymous resident has already taken this up with the Freedom From Religion Foundation. So we shall see how it goes.
         </p>
         <p>
          In the meantime, c
          <a href="http://www.winfieldcity.org/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=62&amp;Itemid=68">
           lick here for the mayor's contact info
          </a>
          so you can ask for God's email address, because I'm sure there are a lot of things on our minds. Things like why does the cable suck, is He looking to flip the property, that sort of thing.
         </p>
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">

           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>
         </div>
         <!-- &lt;h4 id="p_tagErrorMessage"&gt;You must enter at least one Tag for this Diary Entry:&lt;/h4&gt; -->
         <p>
          <input id="p_tagInput" name="tag_draft" size="70" type="text" value=""/>
          <!-- &lt;input id="tagSubmit" type="submit" name="submit" value="Submit" /&gt; -->
         </p>
         <p style="font-style:italic">
          Consider if one or more of these tags fits your diary:
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Civil Rights');return false;">
           Civil Rights
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Community');return false;">
           Community
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Congress');return false;">
           Congress
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Culture');return false;">
           Culture
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Economy');return false;">
           Economy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Education');return false;">
           Education
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Elections');return false;">
           Elections
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Energy');return false;">
           Energy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Environment');return false;">
           Environment
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Health Care');return false;">
           Health Care
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('International');return false;">
           International
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Labor');return false;">
           Labor
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Law');return false;">
           Law
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Media');return false;">
           Media
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Meta');return false;">
           Meta
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('National Security');return false;">
           National Security
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Science');return false;">
           Science
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Transportation');return false;">
           Transportation
          </a>
          , or
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('White House');return false;">
           White House
          </a>
          .
	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('California');return false;">
           California
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Texas');return false;">
           Texas
          </a>
          , etc).
	Keep in mind, though, that there are many wonderful and important diaries
	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.
         </p>
        </div>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             Dear Mayor Price: Please send me Gods e-mail address so I can congratulate her on the acquisition of your town at no cost to her.
            </p>
            <p>
             And also be sure to give Gods e-mail and mailing addresses to your towns property tax collector. You have done a great favor for the people of your town  off loading all their property tax liabilities to God. Will you or God be requiring that they also sign over the deeds to their properties to God? Perhaps that wouldnt sit well with those members of the electorate and other citizens  because the fair market value of the properties is probably greater than their property tax liabilities. So be prepared for some blowback. I hope you are paying for title insurance for Gods ownership because you certainly wouldnt want God coming back to you personally saying she didnt want to pay property taxes for property she did not own in fee and that perhaps you fraudulently gave the property to her.
            </p>
            <p>
             Perhaps you have confused Gods owning souls (of those who willingly give their souls to God) with Gods owning real estate. And you see, even souls must be given willing, not just given to God just by a vote of a bunch of Christian ayatollahs with nothing better to do than violate the 1st Amendment to the U.S. Constitution for fun and a mention on all the satirical programs on TV. You will have your 15 minutes of fame (or, dare I say, infamy) to brag to your grandchildren about.
            </p>
            <p>
             Oh, and while we are talking about the ins- and outs- of real property ownership, I hope your town does not have any restrictive covenants on ownership according to race or color because, as you know, God is black.
            </p>
            <p>
             Cordially,
            </p>

             Scottsdale Bubbe (FYI Bubbe is Grandmother in Yiddish)

            <blockquote>
             REPUBLICAN RED STATES ARE WELFARE QUEENS:
             <p>
              As it turns out, it is red states that are overwhelmingly the Welfare Queen States. Yes, that's right. Red States  the ones governed by folks who think government is too big and spending needs to be cut  are a net drain on the economy, taking in more federal spending than they pay out in federal taxes. They talk a good game, but stick Blue States with the bill.
             </p>
             <p>
              Take a look at the difference between federal spending on any given state and the federal taxes received from that state. We measure the difference as a dollar amount: Federal Spending per Dollar of Federal Taxes. A figure of $1.00 means that particular state received as much as it paid in to the federal government. Anything over a dollar means the state received more than it paid; anything less than $1.00 means the state paid more in taxes than it received in services. The higher the figure, the more a given state is a welfare queen.
             </p>
             <p>
              Of the twenty worst states, 16 are either Republican dominated or conservative states.
             </p>
             <p>
              Go ahead and bookmark this article. The next time some smarmy Tea party buffoon tries to tell you it's liberals who are ruining the country and spending us into oblivion, kindly point them to the evidence that shows it is GOP states, not Democrat states, who are Welfare Queens. It is GOP states who spend more than they collect in taxes. It is GOP states who are out of balance, nationally.
             </p>
             <p>
              See if they still want to cut off funding when it means no more socialism for Republican slave states.
             </p>
             <p>
              <a href="http://www.businessinsider.com/red-states-are-welfare-queens-2011-8">
               http://www.businessinsider.com/...
              </a>
             </p>
            </blockquote>

            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              Hey, there's a good side to this: Jubilee.
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1356520/55375621#c93?mode=alone;showrate=1#c93">
               9+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:145342">
                Carol in San Antonio
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:333891">
                Smoh
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:215040">
                zenbassoon
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:204784">
                blue muon
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:94667">
                edsbrooklyn
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:187444">
                FarWestGirl
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:175114">
                Belle Ame
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:120685">
                happymisanthropy
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:121173">
                Jeff Y
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              So the concept in ancient Israel, at least as perceived by the editors in Ezra's time, was that the land all belonged to YHWH, and he essentially leased it through the parceling to the twelve tribes. That initial division of land gave equal portions to all families.
             </p>
             <p>
              Over time, things became unequal. Some families were better managers. Some were luckier than others. At first, the famlies on hard times sold some of their land to those more successful. Then, they even sold children and occasionally even themselves into slavery.
             </p>
             <p>
              But once every 50 years, things went back to Start. The rich lost all their excess land. The poor regained what had originally been given them. All debt slavery situations were ended.
             </p>
             <p>
              (Now, of course, this was probably the utopian dream of some Iron Age egalitarian. Jeremiah complains that Judah had never implemented this provision.)
             </p>
             <p>
              What I want to know is when does the 50 years begin to run for these Alabamians?
             </p>
             <p>
              Jubilee is on the way, baby!
             </p>
            </div>

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            That God ownes the entire universe. What does he need with a deed to some little town?
           </p>
           <p>
            And what's he going to do with it? Put up a super Walmart? Pave the streets with gold? Make every day Christmas?
           </p>
           <p>
            The silliness of tiny minds.
           </p>

           <li id="c98">
            <div class="cx" id="cx55376000">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               a deed needs to be accepted
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1356520/55376000#c98?mode=alone;showrate=1#c98">
                2+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="crs">
              <dl>
               <dt>
                Recommended by:
               </dt>
               <dd>
                <a href="/user/uid:215040">
                 zenbassoon
                </a>
                ,
                <a href="/user/uid:312579">
                 nuclear winter solstice
                </a>
               </dd>
              </dl>
             </div>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               before the conveyance is complete, in that sense it is very much a contract, an offer of title is made, and accepted by the grantee in the deed, by acts such as recording the deed and entering into possession of the land. In the old days, livery of seisen was frequently done by formally handing over a twig and bit of dirt.
              </p>
              <p>
               To this day there are rare court cases decided on whether there was delivery and acceptance of the deed, such as a parent preparing a deed to a child, never telling anyone, puts it in a safe deposit box, if the child tries to claim the land after the parent's death, other children may successfully challenge delivery and acceptance to defeat the transfer.
              </p>
              <p>
               Boy, are those guys gonna be embarrassed if God doesn't show up to accept the deed.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="cf">
              <p class="sig">
              </p>
              <p class="cb">
               by
               <a href="/user/uid:154504">
                jfromga
               </a>
               on
               <a href="/comments/1356520/55376000#c98">
                Fri Jan 09, 2015 at 07:32:12 AM PST
               </a>
              </p>
              <p class="cl">
               [
               <a href="#c37">
                Parent
               </a>
               ]
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
           </li>
           <ul class="cm i1" id="k55376000">
            <li id="c191">
             <div class="cx" id="cx55389904">
              <h5>
               <a class="de">
               </a>
               <span class="cu">
                Acceptance of deed?
               </span>
               <span class="crd ntb">
                (
                <a href="/comments/1356520/55389904#c191?mode=alone;showrate=1#c191">
                 0+ / 0-
                </a>
                )
               </span>
              </h5>
              <div class="ct">
               <p>
                I don't know what you mean by "acceptance." Perhaps you mean delivery and possession of the deed? In addition, at least here in Arizona, in order for a deed to be complete, it has to be recorded with the county Recorder's office. So the deed in the safe deposit box is not actionable (can't borrow on the property) until the deed is recorded. Title insurance helps, too -- it insures that the person/entity that signed the deed had ownership of the property being conveyed.
               </p>
              </div>
              <div class="cf">
               <p class="sig">
               </p>
               <p class="cb">
                by
                <a href="/user/uid:235149">
                 scottsdalebubbe
                </a>
                on
                <a href="/comments/1356520/55389904#c191">
                 Sat Jan 10, 2015 at 05:50:23 PM PST
                </a>
               </p>
               <p class="cl">
                [
                <a href="#c98">
                 Parent
                </a>
                ]
               </p>
              </div>
             </div>
            </li>
            <ul class="cm i1" id="k55389904">
             <li id="c220">
              <div class="cx" id="cx55402905">
               <h5>
                <a class="de">
                </a>
                <span class="cu">
                 Arizona statutory requirement
                </span>
                <span class="crd ntb">
                 (
                 <a href="/comments/1356520/55402905#c220?mode=alone;showrate=1#c220">
                  0+ / 0-
                 </a>
                 )
                </span>
               </h5>
               <div class="ct">
                <blockquote>
                 33-401. Formal requirements of conveyance; writing; subscription; delivery; acknowledgment; defects
                 <p>
                  A. No estate of inheritance, freehold, or for a term of more than one year, in lands or tenements, shall be conveyed unless the conveyance is by an instrument in writing, subscribed and
                  <strong>
                   delivered
                  </strong>
                  by the party disposing of the estate, or by his agent thereunto authorized by writing.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  B. Every deed or conveyance of real property must be signed by the grantor and must be duly acknowledged before some officer authorized to take acknowledgments.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  C. In every deed or conveyance of real property in which the grantee is subject to regulation pursuant to title 6, 10 or 29, or would be subject to regulation pursuant to title 6, 10 or 29 if doing business in this state, the grantee's name and address and the state in which the grantee is incorporated, organized, licensed, chartered or registered shall be set forth fully, together with the name of the country under which the grantee is chartered or formed. The validity of any deed shall not be affected by any failure to comply with the requirements set forth in this subsection.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  D. For the purposes of this section, a deed or conveyance containing any defect, omission or informality in the certificate of acknowledgment and which has been recorded for longer than ten years in the office of the county recorder of the county in which the property is located shall be deemed to have been duly acknowledged on and after the date of its recording.
                 </p>
                </blockquote>
                case law defining what the statute means by delivery:
                <p>
                 Robinson v. Herring
                 <br/>
                 75 Ariz. 166, 253 P.2d 347
                 <br/>
                 Ariz. 1953
                 <br/>
                </p>
                <blockquote>
                 Plaintiffs cite the case of Parker v. Gentry, 62 Ariz. 115, 154 P.2d 517, in support of their contention that parole evidence is always admissible to prove delivery or non-delivery of a deed, and in that case the court said whether a deed is delivered or not may be proved by parole evidence. This we said did not have the effect of varying the terms of the written instrument.
                 <strong>
                  We further said, to constitute a delivery, there must be not only a delivery but an acceptance and it must appear that the grantor's intention at the time was that **350 the deed should pass title and that he should lose all control over the property conveyed by the terms thereof
                 </strong>
                 . We think this rule applies equally to a lease.
                </blockquote>
                Emphasis added.
                <p>
                 The grantor must wish to convey and the grantee must agree that he/she wants to own the property conveyed. Generally the intentions must be to pass present title, but that can be overcome with an escrow arrangement where the deeds are delivered to a third party for later delivery pursuant to the terms of the agreement. Hence, both parties need to know about the conveyance, and mutually agree that the deed has been delivered to pass title. Hence 'acceptance' is the legal term for the knowing agreement of a grantee to become the new owner (or lienholder) of a property.
                </p>
                <p>
                 Recording is the step that puts the world on notice of the private agreement between the grantor and grantee that title should pass. An unrecorded deed can be effective to pass title, but it may be defeated if another deed is recorded first for the same piece of land in race and race/notice states (race to the courthouse).
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="cf">
                <p class="sig">
                </p>
                <p class="cb">
                 by
                 <a href="/user/uid:154504">
                  jfromga
                 </a>
                 on
                 <a href="/comments/1356520/55402905#c220">
                  Mon Jan 12, 2015 at 12:47:33 PM PST
                 </a>
                </p>
                <p class="cl">
                 [
                 <a href="#c191">
                  Parent
                 </a>
                 ]
                </p>
               </div>
              </div>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </ul>

           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1356520/55374950#c54?mode=alone;showrate=1#c54">
             9+ / 0-

        <li id="c66">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55375077">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            God's Work :: Mule Day
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1356520/55375077#c66?mode=alone;showrate=1#c66">
             5+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:333891">
              Smoh
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:36255">
              liberte
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:34676">
              HeyMikey
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:215040">
              zenbassoon
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:85541">
              old wobbly
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Mule Day 2014 - September 26 - 27, 2014
           </p>
           <p>
            Mule Day 2014
           </p>
           <p>
            2014 marks the 40th year of the Mule Day Festival. The tradition was begun on September 11, 1975, by Curt Estes, Winfield Chamber of Commerce, and Max Brasher, Sr., to honor the hard working mules of the day.
           </p>
           <p>
            Mr. Robert Vickery and Mr. Jack Guin, both from Winfield, were major contributors. No one had any idea this event would grow into the successful event it has become today. Mr Estes lived to see seven Mule Day Parades with an increase in the entries up to 93 in 1983. Since then the participants have increased to nearly triple that number with an estimated crowd of 25,000 spectators. People attend the festival from many parts of the southeast.
           </p>
           <p>
            Our Mule Day founding fathers never dreamed that honoring these hard-working, long-eared mules would have become such a big hit with folks. Well, it did, and these mules love all the attention they receive on this day. So come out and join us in Winfield, Alabama for a great Mule Day celebration.
            <br/>
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">

           </span>

             3+ / 0-

          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            The registered owner of city property in Winfield, Al, a person who goes by the name of "God", received notification of eviction last Tuesday for failure to pay taxes.
           </p>
           <p>
            Several attempts were made by the IRS to contact God at his last known address, but the letters were returned.  An official at the post office acknowledged that the letters had been sent, but commented that the letters were undeliverable, as "Heaven" does not have an official zip code.  Other city officials attempted to pay the taxes in lieu of God, but the IRS would only accept payment from the registered property owner.
           </p>
           <p>
            One city official was quoted as saying, "It's in God's hands now."

           <p>

           <p>
            Who remembers an earlier America that feared JFK might be incapable of thinking independently of the Vatican?
           </p>
           <p>
            How far America has declined. (Sigh) Friends in Canada and Europe say that if their politicians crowed in public about their "personal relationship with Jesus" it would mark the end of their political future.
           </p>

           </p>
           <p>
            For the past 50+ years, Americans have tolerated religious entanglement in politics, despite the fact that the 1st Amendment forbids it. This instant report is an example of exactly the kind of insanity the 1st Amendment was created to avoid.
           </p>
           <p>
            This entanglement is extremely troubling. The 2016 GOP hopefuls are downright scary! While I'd love to have the confidence to think the GOP candidates for POTUS make a Democratic win a near certainty, I know how fickle Americans are.
           </p>
           <p>
            Who would believe that we would elect a Republican majority for Congress less than a decade after Republican policies nearly triggered the 2nd Great Depression?! You see, I'm just not convinced Americans are smart enough to avoid electing a theocrat. That's
            <em>
             frightening
            </em>
            .
           </p>
           <p>
            I don't believe there are easy answers, but what I do know is that we'd better get our shite together.

        </li>
        <ul class="cm i1" id="k55385995">
         <li id="c198">
          <div class="cx" id="cx55390308">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             The legal term
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1356520/55390308#c198?mode=alone;showrate=1#c198">
              0+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             for what you are suggesting is filing of a "Lis Pendens" with the court and, once the judge approves the Lis Pendens, filing it in the property records of whatever municipality or county retains property records. It means that the property owner, whoever he, she or it (one of those corporate "persons") may be, must clear the claims of the Lis Pendens before he, she, or it can lease, sell, or hypothecate (get a loan) the property. All commerce in regard to that property ceases and no title insurance company will insure ownership until the Lis Pendens is removed by court order.
            </p>
           </div>

        <li id="c178">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55388790">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            This wouldn't be a problem if...
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1356520/55388790#c178?mode=alone;showrate=1#c178">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Whereas, we acknowledge that though prayer, with His guidance and presence, that we will be able to trust that no problem will be too large or too small to overcome."
           </p>
           <p>
            Trusting that no problem is too big or too small is a lovely, positive sentiment, and a vow to heed the guidance of God wouldn't be a problem if one believed that 1) these persons unfailingly understood that guidance and 2) were actually acting on that and not their own desires, fears, phobias, and prejudices.
           </p>
           <p>
            But the track record of human beings (especially those in power) of heeding the guidance in any of the world's scriptures (which are startlingly consonant) is pretty abysmal. In a word, we suck at doing God's will. We get hung up in dogmatic formulae and forget that the emphasis in every one of these allegedly "different" religions is love of, service to, and unity with our fellow human beings.
           </p>
           <p>
            How else do we explain misogyny, homophobia, racism, fanatical hatred of this or that "other" group when contrasted to messages many of us claim to believe are divine in origin that tell us to love our neighborseven those we think of as 'not us'love even our enemies, give without hoping for repayment or reward, prefer the welfare of our fellow human beings to our own? How do we explain the visceral hatred shown to illegal immigrants in light of guidance to befriend the stranger and refugee, to raise up the poor, show kindness to the imprisoned, feed the starving, heal the sick?
           </p>
           <p>
            Vowing to heed the guidance from God would be laudable if we actually could be trust to carry through instead of cherry picking scripture looking for loopholes that would make just a little injustice okay.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">

           <p>
            Will they send the tax bills to god? What is his address? As the owner of record, he would be liable for repairs and subject to being sued for damages for injuries caused by failure to maintain his property. Has he appointed an agent to enter contracts for him and to receive service? Since the town has decided to cede ownership, the mayor et al may no longer have the authority to act on matters concerning the town if god didn't give them power of attorney to act in his name. (Can't wait to see who notarizes that little gem.)
           </p>
           <p>
            Some times publicity stunts backfire and this looks like one of them. By ceding ownership, with all the responsibilities that entails to an imaginary sky being, the mayor has created a host of legal issues for himself and the town. Just dying to see a suit brought by a contractor who did work for the city and didn't get paid. A municipality or other government creation may be exempt from law suits arising from their performance or failure to perform in governing said entity. There is no such exemption for a deity.
           </p>
           <p>
            In fact since the town is now officially god's property, that would make it the perfect place for those wishing to sue the deity for any problem. Basic law, an entity, usually a corporation or person, can be sued in any state where the offense occurred or where the entity owns property. Got a beef with god, ask for a lien on his town.

            </strong>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             We believe in one God,
             <br/>
             the Father, the Almighty,
             <br/>
             maker of heaven and earth,
             <br/>
             of all that is, seen and unseen.
             <br/>
             We believe in one Lord, Jesus Christ,
             <br/>
             the only Son of God,
             <br/>
             eternally begotten of the Father,
             <br/>
             God from God, Light from Light,
             <br/>
             true God from true God,
             <br/>
             begotten, not made,
             <br/>
             of one Being with the Father.
             <br/>
             Through him all things were made.
             <br/>
             For us and for our salvation
             <br/>
             he came down from heaven:
             <br/>
             by the power of the Holy Spirit
             <br/>
             he became incarnate from the Virgin Mary,
             <br/>
             and was made man.
             <br/>
             For our sake he was crucified under Pontius Pilate;
             <br/>
             he suffered death and was buried.
             <br/>
             On the third day he rose again
             <br/>
             in accordance with the Scriptures;
             <br/>
             he ascended into heaven
             <br/>
             and is seated at the right hand of the Father.
             <br/>
             He will come again in glory to judge the living and the dead,
             <br/>
             and his kingdom will have no end.
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             We believe in the Holy Spirit, the Lord, the giver of life,
             <br/>
             who proceeds from the Father and the Son.
             <br/>
             With the Father and the Son he is worshiped and glorified.
             <br/>
             He has spoken through the Prophets.
             <br/>
             We believe in one holy catholic and apostolic Church.
             <br/>
             We acknowledge one baptism for the forgiveness of sins.
             <br/>
             We look for the resurrection of the dead,
             <br/>
             and the life of the world to come. Amen.
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            As a Catholic, this is what I believe. However, the proclamation from city leaders in Winfield, Alabama has
            <strong>
             no place whatsoever
            </strong>
            in government. For a city to cede its ownership to God not only goes against the U.S. Constitution, it's just downright ridiculous. Yes, as a Roman Catholic, I believe in the Apostle's Creed. However, I also believe in the separation of Church and State. For real, these people are just plumb, batcrap crazy.

           </p>

        <li class="from-mobile" id="c219">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55398897">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Well that's one town that is officially off the...
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1356520/55398897#c219?mode=alone;showrate=1#c219">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Well that's one town that is officially off the welfare and corporate subsidy teats... God provides, and all that.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            Now we just need a few other people (and by people I mean 'corporate entities') to sign over their holdings to God, so we can stop paying them subsidies too.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:993243">
             dcnblues
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1356520/55398897#c219">
             Sun Jan 11, 2015 at 09:43:36 PM PST
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </li>
        <li id="c221">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55404818">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Did I miss it...
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1356520/55404818#c221?mode=alone;showrate=1#c221">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            ...or is nobody else bugged by the fact that (in addition to the silliness of the theism involved) there's no actual resolution there?
           </p>
           <p>
            They've got a bunch of "Whereas" clauses, and no "it is resolved" punchline...
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:27181">
             nkedel
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1356520/55404818#c221">
             Mon Jan 12, 2015 at 05:14:12 PM PST
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>

   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {

		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() {

		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}

		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {

		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
  </script>
  <!-- end mixpanel -->
 </body>
</html>
